her freak be painful to witness and difficult to control
it begin to be say in the country that the countess be go mad
my scoundrelly enemy do not fail to confirm and magnify the rumour and would add that i be the cause of her insanity i have drive she to distraction i have kill bullingdon i have murder my own son i donot know what else they lay to my charge
even in ireland their hateful calumny reach i my friend fall away from i
they begin to desert my hunt as they do in england and when i go to race or market find sudden reason for get out of my neighbourhood
i get the name of wicked barry devil lyndon which you please the country- folk use to make marvellous legend about i the priest say i have massacre i donot know how many german nun in the seven years war that the ghost of the murder bullingdon haunt my house
once at a fair in a town hard by when i have a mind to buy a waistcoat for one of my people a fellow standing by say tis a strait-waistcoat hebe buy for my lady lyndon and from this circumstance arise a legend of my cruelty to my wife and many circumstantial detail be narrate regard my manner and ingenuity of torture she
the loss of my dear boy press not only on my heart as a father but injure my individual interest in a very considerable degree for as there be now no direct heir to the estate and lady lyndon be of a weak health and suppose to be quite unlikely to leave a family the next in succession-that detestable family of tiptoff-- begin to exert themselves in a hundred way to annoy i and be at the head of the party of enemy who be raise report to my discredit
they interpose between i and my management of the property in a hundred different way make an outcry if i cut a stick sink a shaft sell a picture or send a few ounce of plate to be remodelle
they harass i with ceaseless lawsuit get injunction from chancery hamper my agent in the execution of their work so much so that you would have fancy my own be not my own but theirs to do as they like with
what be bad as i have reason to believe they have tampering and dealing with my own domestic under my own roof for i could not have a word with lady lyndon but it somehow get abroad and i could not be drunk with my chaplain and friend but some sanctify rascal would get hold of the news and reckon up all the bottle i drink and all the oath i swear
that these be not few i acknowledge
i be of the old school be always a free liver and speaker and at least if i do and say what i like be not so bad as many a cant scoundrel i know of who cover his foible and sin unsuspected with a mask of holiness
as i be make a clean breast of it and be no hypocrite i may as well confess now that i endeavour to ward off the device of my enemy by an artifice which be not perhaps strictly justifiable
everything depend on my have an heir to the estate for if lady lyndon who be of weakly health have die the next day i be a beggar all my sacrifice of money c on the estate would not have be hold in a farthing s account all the debt would have be leave on my shoulder and my enemy would have triumph over i which to a man of my honourable spirit be the unkind cut of all as some poet say
i confess then it be my wish to supplant these scoundrel and as i could not do so without an heir to my property i determined to find one
if i have he near at hand and of my own blood too though with the bar sinister be not here the question
it be then i find out the rascally machination of my enemy for have broach this plan to lady lyndon whom i make to be outwardly at least the most obedient of wives although i never let a letter from she or to she go or arrive without my inspection although i allow she to see none but those person who i think in her delicate health would be fitting society for she yet the infernal tiptoff get wind of my scheme protest instantly against it not only by letter but in the shameful libellous public print and hold i up to public odium as a child-forger as they call i
of course i deny the charge--i could do no otherwise and offer to meet any one of the tiptoffs on the field of honour and prove he a scoundrel and a liar as he be though perhaps not in this instance
but they content themselves by answer i by a lawyer and decline an invitation which any man of spirit would have accept
my hope of have an heir be thus blight completely indeed lady lyndon though as i have say i take her opposition for nothing have resist the proposal with as much energy as a woman of her weakness could manif and say she have commit one great crime in consequence of i but would rather die than perform another
i could easily have bring her ladyship to her sens however but my scheme have take wind and it be now in vain to attempt it
we might have have a dozen child in honest wedlock and people would have say they be false
as for raise money on annuity i may say i have use her life interest up
there be but few of those assurance society in my time which have since spring up in the city of london underwriter do the business and my wife s life be as well know among they as i do believe that of any woman in christendom
latterly when i want to get a sum against her life the rascal have the impudence to say my treatment of she do not render it worth a year s purchase a if my interest lie in kill she
have my boy live it would have be a different thing he and his mother might have cut off the entail of a good part of the property between they and my affair have be put in well order
now they be in a bad condition indeed
all my scheme have turn out failure my land which i have purchase with borrow money make i no return and i be oblige to pay ruinous interest for the sum with which i have purchase they
my income though very large be saddle with hundred of annuity and thousand of lawyer charge and i feel the net draw close and close round i and no mean to extricate myself from its toil
to add to all my perplexity two year after my poor child s death my wife whose vagary of temper and wayward folly i have bear with for twelve year want to leave i and absolutely make attempt at what she call escape from my tyranny
my mother who be the only person that in my misfortune remain faithful to i indeed she have always speak of i in my true light as a martyr to the rascality of other and a victim of my own generous and confide temper find out the first scheme that be go on and of which those artful and malicious tiptoff be as usual the main promoter
mrs
barry indeed though her temper be violent and her way singular be an invaluable person to i in my house which would have be at rack and ruin long before but for her spirit of order and management and for her excellent economy in the government of my numerous family
as for my lady lyndon she poor soul
be much too fine a lady to attend to household matters-- pass her day with her doctor or her book of piety and never appear among we except at my compulsion when she and my mother would be sure to have a quarrel
mrs
barry on the contrary have a talent for management in all matter
she keep the maid stir and the footman to their duty have an eye over the claret in the cellar and the oats and hay in the stable see to the salting and pickling the potato and the turf-stacking the pig-killing and the poultry the linen-room and the bakehouse and the ten thousand minutia of a great establishment
if all irish housewife be like she i warrant many a hall-fire would be blaze where the cobwebs only grow now and many a park cover with sheep and fat cattle where the thistle be at present the chief occupier
if anything could have save i from the consequence of villainy in other and i confess it for i be not above own to my fault my own too easy generous and careless nature it would have be the admirable prudence of that worthy creature
she never go to bed until all the house be quiet and all the candle out and you may fancy that this be a matter of some difficulty with a man of my habit who have commonly a dozen of jovial fellow artful scoundrel and false friend most of they be to drink with i every night and who seldom for my part go to bed sober
many and many a night when i be unconscious of her attention have that good soul pull my boot off and see i lay by my servant snug in bed and carry off the candle herself and be the first in the morning too to bring i my drink of small-beer
mine be no milksop time i can tell you
a gentleman think no shame of take his half-dozen bottle and as for your coffee and slop they be leave to lady lyndon her doctor and the other old woman
it be my mother s pride that i could drink more than any man in the country as much within a pint as my father before i she say
that lady lyndon should detest she be quite natural
she be not the first of woman or mankind either that have hat a mother-in-law
i set my mother to keep a sharp watch over the freak of her ladyship and this you may be sure be one of the reason why the latter dislike she
i never mind that however
mrs
barry s assistance and surveillance be invaluable to i and if i have pay twenty spy to watch my lady i should not have be half so well serve as by the disinterested care and watchfulness of my excellent mother
she sleep with the house-key under her pillow and have an eye everywhere

this give the lie to any of those maligner who say i wish to make a prisoner of my wife
the fact be that know her levity and see the insane dislike to i and mine which have now begin to supersede what perhaps have be an equally insane fondness for i i be bind to be on my guard that she should not give i the slip

this which my mother know compel we to keep a tight watch over she but as for imprison she i repel the imputation with scorn
every man imprison his wife to a certain degree the world would be in a pretty condition if woman be allow to quit home and return to it whenever they have a mind
in watch over my wife lady lyndon i do no more than exercise the legitimate authority which award honour and obedience to every husband

one would have think that follow as she be all her letter read and all her acquaintance strictly watch by i live in a remote part of ireland away from her family lady lyndon could have have no chance of communicate with her ally or of make her wrong as she be pleased to call they public and yet for a while she carry on a correspondence under my very nose and acutely organise a conspiracy for fly from i as shall be tell

i will give a speciman of one of the horrid artful letter of this unhappy woman

so the letter would run on for sheet upon sheet in the close cramp handwriting and i leave any unprejudiced reader to say whether the writer of such document must not have be as silly and vain a creature as ever live and whether she do not want be take care of

one of my collier have a pretty daughter and this pretty lass have for her bachelor as they call they in ireland a certain lad who bring the letter-bag for castle lyndon and many a dunning letter for i be there in it god wot this letter-boy tell his sweetheart how he bring a bag of money from the town for master quin and how that tim the post-boy have tell he that he be to bring a chaise down to the water at a certain hour
miss rooney who have no secret from i blurt out the whole story ask i what scheme i be after and what poor unlucky girl i be go to carry away with the chaise i have order and bribe with the money i have get from town
